!Series_title	"Transcriptome profiling of the normal breast of women at either high- or average risk for breast cancer [RNA-Seq]"
!Series_geo_accession	"GSE164641"
!Series_status	"Public on Sep 30 2021"
!Series_submission_date	"Jan 12 2021"
!Series_last_update_date	"Feb 18 2022"
!Series_pubmed_id	"35139887"
!Series_summary	"Epigenetic mechanisms such as DNA methylation are important regulators of gene expression and are frequently dysregulated early in breast carcinogenesis. The relationship between DNA methylation aberrations in normal breast tissue and breast cancer risk remains unclear. Disease-free breast tissue cores donated by  high-risk (Tyrer-Cuzick lifetime risk ≥20%) and 78 average-risk women were obtained from the Susan G. Komen Tissue Bank and processed for whole methylome and whole transcriptome profiling. We identified 1355 CpGs that were differentially methylated between high- and average-risk breast tissues (ΔZ>0.5, FDR<0.05). Hypomethylated CpGs were overrepresented in high-risk tissue and were found predominantly (68%) in non-coding regions. Hypermethylated CpG sites were found equally in the gene body and non-coding regions. Transcriptomic analysis identified 67 differentially expressed genes (fold change≥2, FDR<0.05, 17 down 50 up), involved in chemokines signaling, metabolism and estrogen biosynthesis. Methylation-expression correlations revealed 6 epigenetically regulated genes in high-risk breast. This is the first gene expression/DNA methylation analysis of normal breasts from women at either high or average risk of breast cancer. Our discovery of epigenetically regulated genes associated with breast cancer risk using a unique resource of normal breast samples opens the doors to a deeper understanding of the process of cancer initiation and provides an opportunity to mechanistically dissect breast cancer susceptibility and risk-associated molecular alterations."
!Series_overall_design	"The study cohorts includes 165  women at either  average or high risk for breast cancer according to the Tyrer Cuzick risk assessment score.  Fresh frozen breast tssue cores were processed for  RNA/DNA extraction. Methyl-capture was then employed to obtain the methylome profiling, while RNAseq was used to obtain the transcriptome profing of each sample"
!Series_type	"Expression profiling by high throughput sequencing"

!Sample_growth_protocol_ch1	"The breast tissue cores are collected by using a needle biopsy needle (Hologic, Marlborough, MA). The skin is cleaned, then numbed with lidocaine. The physician nicks the skin with a scalpel, usually in the upper-outer quadrant of the breast, and the needle is inserted into this incision. From this single incision, five sample cores are removed from the breast (approximately 200mg). A nurse/surgeon’s assistant holds pressure on the incision for 10 full minutes, then applies a pressure bandage. An ice pack is immediately placed on the breast. Within 10 min from collection the tissue cores are fresh frozen in liquid nitrogen"	"The breast tissue cores are collected by using a needle biopsy needle (Hologic, Marlborough, MA). A nurse/surgeon’s assistant holds pressure on the incision for 10 full minutes, then applies a pressure bandage. An ice pack is immediately placed on the breast. !Sample_extract_protocol_ch1	"The concentration and quality of total RNA and DNA samples was first assessed using Agilent 2100 Bioanalyzer. For the RNAsequencing: cDNA library was prepared using the TruSeq Stranded Total RNA Kit (Illumina) and sequenced using Illumina HiSeq4000.
